⏺ 基础匹配阶段完整书稿 7 秒、缓存命中 6.7
  秒，相比旧版 3 小时快了约 1500
  倍。下面写一份运行说明和验收清单：

⏺ Write(/Users/wangyubo/github-resp/quote-check-v2/RE
       ADME.md)
  ⎿  Added 60 lines, removed 2 lines
       1  # 黑猫核校
       2 -本项目实现书稿引文核校功能。用户提供
         -10万到30万字书稿，100万到300万字参考
         -文献，本程序解析出书稿中所有引用原文
         -、引文注释、引用上下文段落，并使用程
         -序、大模型与参考文献原文及解释比对，
         -核校该引文、引文注释是否与原文字词句
         -一致，是否意思一致、是否使用正确。
       2
       4 -书稿和参考文献支持docx、txt、pdf（非
         -扫描版pdf）。
       3 +中文古籍引文核校工具。给定书稿（docx
         +/txt/pdf）与参考文献，自动验证书稿中
         +的引文是否忠实于原文，输出 A/B/C/D
         +四级判定报告。
       4 +
       5 +## 性能
       6 +
       7 +| 数据规模 | 旧版 | 当前 |
       8 +|---|---|---|
       9 +| 10 万字书稿 + 200 万字参考文献（9
         +部古籍） | ~3 小时 | **~7 秒**（首次
         +）/ **~6.7 秒**（索引缓存命中） |
      10 +
      11 +不含 LLM 阶段。LLM 阶段（仅对疑难引
         +文调用）预计再增加 10-30 秒。
      12 +
      13 +## 安装
      14 +
      15 +```bash
      16 +uv sync
      17 +```
      18 +
      19 +## 使用
      20 +
      21 +```bash
      22 +# 仅字面层判定（快速预览，不调 LLM）
      23 +uv run python cli.py check manuscrip
         +t/书稿.docx --bib bib/*.txt --no-llm
         + --out report.md
      24 +
      25 +# 完整核校（含 LLM 语义判定）
      26 +export SILICONFLOW_API_KEY=sk-xxx
      27 +uv run python cli.py check manuscrip
         +t/书稿.docx --bib bib/*.txt --out re
         +port.md
      28 +
      29 +# 输出 HTML / JSON
      30 +uv run python cli.py check ... --fmt
         + html --out report.html
      31 +uv run python cli.py check ... --fmt
         + json --out report.json
      32 +```
      33 +
      34 +支持格式：`docx` / `txt` / `pdf`（非
         +扫描版）。
      35 +
      36 +## 报告分级
      37 +
      38 +- **A 完全一致** — 字符级与原文一致
         +，或仅标点/异体字差异
      39 +- **B 轻微差异不影响意义** — 异体字
         +、通假字、可接受的格式差异
      40 +- **C 文字或意义可能有问题** — 缺字/
         +多字/换字，需人工复核
      41 +- **D 无法定位来源 / 疑似错引** — 在
         +所有参考文献中未找到对应原文
      42 +
      43 +## 架构
      44 +
      45 +```
      46 +core/api.py        ← 唯一对外入口 ch
         +eck()
      47 +core/parse.py      文档解析（docx/tx
         +t/pdf）
      48 +core/extract.py    引文抽取（引号/书
         +名号/脚注 3 路）
      49 +core/normalize.py  归一化（繁简/异体
         +字/标点）
      50 +core/index.py      5-gram 倒排索引 +
         + sha256 磁盘缓存
      51 +core/match.py      三阶段核验（精确→
         +模糊→diff）
      52 +core/llm.py        SiliconFlow LLM
         +客户端（仅对疑难项调用）
      53 +core/report.py     报告渲染（md / ht
         +ml / json）
      54 +core/bib/          bib 解析器插件（
         +注册表 + 分书 parser）
      55 +cli.py             CLI 薄壳
      56 +```
      57 +
      58 +详细设计见 `~/.claude/plans/10-90-3-
         +flickering-patterson.md`。
      59 +
      60 +## 后续 Web 化
      61 +
      62 +`core.api.check()` 是同步函数 + on_p
         +rogress 回调，可直接在 FastAPI + RQ
         +后台任务中复用，无需重写核心。

        import zipfile, re
        from xml.etree import ElementTree as ET
        with zipfile.ZipFile('manuscript/幺弟解惑-部
  分章节.docx') as z:
            with z.open('word/document.xml') as f:
                data = f.read().decode('utf-8',
  errors='ignore')
        text = re.sub(r'<[^>]+>', '', data)

       First 2000:  仅以此书，献给亲爱的幺弟，及喜爱
  幺弟的朋友们！读书篇01

  为什么中华文明能传承数千年？爸爸：幺弟，为什么我们
  中华文明能传承几千年，而其他古文明没能传承那么久

  ？幺弟：我们中华文明能传承这么久，汉字功不可没。《
  道德经》说“惚兮恍兮，其中有象”，像“道”一样模糊不

  清，但是其中有“象”，我们的汉字就是把“道”中那些“象”
  和“物”直接化成了字。比如“日、月、山、水”，看见“日

  ”这个字就知道是“太阳”，看见“山”这个字就晓得是“山”
  。汉字把老子说的“恍之道”用“象”固定下来，即使穿越时

  空，这个字还是能被认识。其他文明主要用的是拼音文字
  语言，文字组合一变化就成了天书了，而汉字就像“活化

  石”，不管隔多久都能被认识。《易经》都说：“书不尽言
  ，言不尽意”，文字写不完语言，语言说不尽思想。就是

  因为汉字把我们中国天南地北的人联系在一起，不管是朝
  代更替还是方言不同，只要“字”在，我们的思想就能连

  在一起。爸爸你看，过了一千多年了，为什么现在我们还
  能看懂《黄帝内经》，能看懂《伤寒论》？都是因为汉

  字的功劳！要是换成拼音文字早就读不懂了。其实真的该
  给其他国家提一个建议，让每个国家把自己的科技文明

  和历史都用汉字备份一下，免得自己的文明过了很多年失
  传。你想想，如果没有汉字，诸子百家就只能昙花一现
       ，《道德经》就成了天书，汉字就是中华文明藏在
  天地中的“源代码”呀！
  注释:“惚兮恍兮，其中有象”，出自老

  子《道德经》第二十一章，原文为：“孔德之容，惟道是
  从。道之为物，惟恍惟惚。惚兮恍兮，其中有象；恍兮惚

  兮，其中有物。”这一描述体现了道家对“道”的哲学理解
  。“惚”指模糊不清，“恍”指隐约闪烁，形容“道”看似恍恍
       惚惚，若有若无的样子。‌象‌：指道的显现形式‌。‌物‌
  ：是道的具体化产物‌。“惚兮

      from core.parse import parse
      from core.extract import extract
      from core.index import build_corpus
      from core.match import match
      from core.llm import LLMClient

      parse('manuscript/幺弟解惑-部分章节.docx')

      corpus =
      build_corpus(sorted(Path('bib').glob('*.txt')))
      llm = LLMClient(api_key='$SILICONFLOW_API_KEY')

      for v in verdicts:

  from verdicts
  - When _judge_one_batch modifies batch[rid], it
  modifies the targets list element, which is the

  The first batch took 233s. That's very suspicious.
  Let me look at the actual _judge_one_batch
  function's error handling. If the first batch had a
   timeout or error, the exception handler would mark
   all targets as failed but would NOT modify the
  batch items.

  Let me re-read the exception handling in
  judge_batch:

  for fut in _cf.as_completed(futs):
      try:
          fut.result()  # _judge_one_batch
  内部已就地修改 Verdict
      except Exception as e:
          for v in targets:
              if v.needs_llm:
                  v.issues.append(f"LLM 失败: {e}")
                  v.needs_llm = False

  There's a problem here! _cf.as_completed — this is
  concurrent.futures.as_completed. But futs is
  created with pool.submit(_judge_one_batch, batch,
  llm). When the first future returns (possibly with
  an error), the except block iterates for v in
  targets and marks ALL targets as failed! This would
   explain why all items still have needs_llm=True —
  no wait, it sets needs_llm=False.

  def _judge_one_batch(batch: list[Verdict], llm:
  LLMClient) -> None:
      payload = []
      for i, v in enumerate(batch):
          item = {
              "id": i,
              ...
          }

  + json.dumps(payload, ensure_ascii=False)
      parsed = llm.chat_json(_SYSTEM_PROMPT, user)

  The test output showed 34 items needed LLM across 5

  (ceil). Let me check what the LLM actually returns.
   The smoke test returned a single dict, but the
  batch call expects a list of dicts.

  Actually, I think I found the bug. Looking at the
  prompt format:

  user = f"请判定下列 {len(payload)} 条引文：\n" +
  json.dumps(payload, ensure_ascii=False)
  parsed = llm.chat_json(_SYSTEM_PROMPT, user)

  The chat_json method uses response_format={"type":
  "json_object"} which forces the LLM to return a
  JSON object (not array). The system prompt asks for
   an array, but json_object mode in
  OpenAI-compatible APIs requires the top-level to be
   an object, not an array!

  So the LLM wraps the array in {"results": [...]} or
   similar. The code handles this:
  if isinstance(parsed, dict):
      for k in ("results", "verdicts", "data",
  "items"):
          if k in parsed and isinstance(parsed[k],
  list):
              parsed = parsed[k]
              break

  But what if the LLM uses a different key name? Like
   "verdicts" or something else? If none of the known
   keys match, the code falls through to:
  list_vals = [v for v in parsed.values() if
  isinstance(v, list)]
  parsed = list_vals[0] if list_vals else []

  If list_vals is empty (no list values in the dict),
   then parsed = [], and the for loop for r in
  parsed: doesn't execute, so no verdicts are
  updated!

  That's likely the bug. Let me check what the LLM
  actually returns for a batch call.

⏺ LLM 结果没有应用。needs_llm 仍为 True，说明
  _judge_one_batch 返回了解析失败。让我调试 LLM
  响应格式。

      print()

      if isinstance(parsed, dict):
          print('Keys:', list(parsed.keys()))
          for k, v in parsed.items():
              if isinstance(v, list):
                  print(f'  {k}: list of {len(v)}
      items')
                  if v:
                      print(f'    first item keys:
      {list(v[0].keys()) if isinstance(v[0], dict)
      else type(v[0]).__name__}')

  Hold on — maybe there's a subtle issue. The targets
   list is created as [v for v in verdicts if
  v.needs_llm], and batch = targets[i:i+batch_size].
  The items in batch are the SAME Verdict objects as
  in verdicts. So _apply_llm_result(batch[rid], r)
  modifies the original Verdict object.

  Unless... the batch is passed to
  pool.submit(_judge_one_batch, batch, llm) — this
  serializes the batch to send to the worker thread.
  In Python's ThreadPoolExecutor, objects are NOT
  serialized (threads share memory). So the same
  Verdict objects should be accessible.

  Wait, actually, maybe the issue is that the first
  batch timed out and the exception handler ran. Let
  me check: the first batch took 233s. If it timed
  out, the exception handler would mark ALL targets
  as failed — but the handler sets needs_llm = False,
   and my test shows needs_llm = True. So either:
  1. The first batch didn't time out (233s is just
  SiliconFlow being slow)
  2. Something else is going on

  Actually, wait — _cf.as_completed(futs) iterates as
   futures complete. If the first future completes
  successfully (takes 233s), fut.result() returns
  None (since _judge_one_batch returns None). Then
  done += 1 and we move to the next future.

  But here's the thing: the 5 futures are submitted
  to a thread pool with max_workers=4. The first one
  takes 233s. The other 4 are waiting in the queue.
  But they're all processing different batches. After
   the first one completes, the others complete
  quickly (2-13s each).

  So the flow should be:
  1. All 5 batches submitted to pool (max_workers=4,
  so 4 run immediately, 1 queued)
  2. Batch 1 completes after 233s → done=1
  3. The queued batch runs, completes in 2s → done=2
  4. etc.

  All batches should complete successfully. So
  _apply_llm_result should be called. But it isn't.
  Let me think about what else could go wrong...

  Wait! I just realized — the debug test that I ran
  was a SEPARATE Python process. It created a NEW
  LLMClient with the API key. But the CLI invocation
  (cli.py check ...) works differently — it uses
  core.api.check() which internally calls match()
  with the LLM client.

  Actually, the simpler approach: when --no-llm, pass
   None. When not --no-llm, pass None too, and let
  _make_llm read from env. The current code
  llm_key=None if args.no_llm else None already does
  this. So the issue wasn't actually in cli.py.

  But wait, there's a subtle issue. If the user
  explicitly set SILICONFLOW_API_KEY in their env and
   passes --no-llm, we want llm_key=None. Currently,
  llm_key=None if args.no_llm else None gives None in
   both cases, which is correct. _make_llm with
  key=None will check the env var and find it. So
  --no-llm would still invoke LLM!

  The fix should be: when --no-llm, explicitly pass
  something that prevents LLM. The cleanest approach:
  - --no-llm → llm_key=False or something
  - No --no-llm → llm_key=None (read from env)

  Actually, looking at _make_llm:
  def _make_llm(key: str | None, model: str,
  base_url: str, warnings: list[str]):
      key = key or
  os.environ.get("SILICONFLOW_API_KEY")
      if not key:
          return None

  So key=None → reads from env. If env is set, LLM is
   used even with --no-llm.

  The fix should be to handle --no-llm differently.

  something that won't trigger the env fallback. Or

      _API_KEY'])

      print(f'With LLM: {elapsed:.1f}s')

  Now I can see: only 2 out of 34 items got their
  needs_llm set to False! And 32 items still have
  needs_llm=True. This means the LLM processed only
  some of the items and missed most of them.

  The likely issue: the LLM returns results for some
  items but not all, or the rid (id) values in the
  LLM response don't match the batch indices.

  Let me check what's happening. The batch size is 8.
   With 34 items: 5 batches (8+8+8+8+2). The first
  batch takes super long (233s in the earlier run).
  The other batches complete faster. But most items
  don't get their needs_llm flag cleared.

  Wait, looking at the code flow again:

  targets: list[Verdict] = [v for v in verdicts if
  v.needs_llm]
  batches = [targets[i : i + batch_size] for i in
  range(0, len(targets), batch_size)]
  # batches = [targets[0:8], targets[8:16],
  targets[16:24], targets[24:32], targets[32:34]]

  With _cf.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=4):
  - 4 workers process 4 batches at a time
  - If the first batch takes 233s and the others take
   2-13s, the other 3 finish quickly
  - Then the 5th batch runs and finishes

  But the output shows only 2 items changed. That
  means only the first batch (or whichever batch the
  2 changed items were in) actually applied results.

  The key issue is probably in _judge_one_batch — the
   LLM might be returning results with incorrect IDs,
   or the LLM might be processing items correctly but
   the _apply_llm_result function isn't matching the
  verdict string.

  Wait, let me look at this more carefully. The 2
  changed items are both from note[72]. They have
  grade=D. The LLM kept them at D but added
  suggestion and issues. So _apply_llm_result worked
  for those 2 items.

  The remaining 32 items are unchanged. Let me think
  about why...

  Oh! I think the issue is the _cf.ThreadPoolExecutor
   + _cf.as_completed. Let me look at this:
  with
  _cf.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=max_workers) as
  pool:
      futs = [pool.submit(_judge_one_batch, batch,
  llm) for batch in batches]
      for fut in _cf.as_completed(futs):

  The for fut in _cf.as_completed(futs) iterates in
  completion order. When a future completes,
  fut.result() is called. If _judge_one_batch raises
  an exception, the except block marks all targets as
   failed. But what if some batches are STILL RUNNING
   when the exception occurs?

  Let me look at this flow more carefully. With 5
  batches and 4 workers:
  1. Batches 0, 1, 2, 3 start (4 workers)
  2. Batch 0 takes 233s to complete → done=1
  3. After batch 0 completes, batch 4 starts
  4. Batches 1, 2, 3 complete quickly (2-13s) →
  done=2, 3, 4
  5. Batch 4 completes → done=5

  But what if there's an issue with how the Python
  objects are shared between threads? In CPython,
  there's no serialization for thread pool. The same
  objects should be accessible.

  Actually, I wonder if the issue is with _cf import.
   Let me check:
  import concurrent.futures as _cf

  And then _cf.as_completed — this is fine.
  _cf.ThreadPoolExecutor — also fine.

  Wait, _cf.as_completed might not be the standard
  way to iterate. Let me check... actually
  concurrent.futures.as_completed is the standard
  function. And _cf.as_completed(futs) should work
  correctly.

      print(f'Type: {type(parsed).__name__}')
      if isinstance(parsed, dict):
          print(f'Keys: {list(parsed.keys())}')
          for k, v in parsed.items():
              if isinstance(v, list):
                  print(f'{k}: list of {len(v)}')

                      print(f'  {item}')

  ⎿  (timeout 10m)

∴ Thinking…

  Found it! The LLM is returning a single dict like
  {'id': 0, 'verdict': '...', 'issues': [...], ...}
  instead of wrapping it in {'results': [{'id': 0,
  ...}, ...]}.

  The issue is in the json_object response format.
  When you use response_format={"type":
  "json_object"}, the API forces the LLM to output
  valid JSON, but NOT necessarily wrapping in
  {"results": [...]}. The system prompt says "输出
  JSON 数组" but the json_object mode restricts to
  objects, not arrays. So some LLMs output a single
  flat object instead.

  Looking at the code flow:
  1. chat_json returns {'id': 0, 'verdict':
  'FAITHFUL', ...}
  2. In _judge_one_batch:
  if isinstance(parsed, dict):
      for k in ("results", "verdicts", "data",
  "items"):
          if k in parsed and isinstance(parsed[k],
  list):
              parsed = parsed[k]
              break
      else:
          # 取唯一的列表值
          list_vals = [v for v in parsed.values() if
  isinstance(v, list)]
          parsed = list_vals[0] if list_vals else []
  3. The dict has keys ['id', 'verdict', 'issues',
  'suggestion', 'confidence']
  4. None of ("results", "verdicts", "data", "items")
   match as list values
  5. list_vals checks for list values in the dict →
  none found (all values are strings/int/floats)
  6. parsed = []
  7. for r in parsed: → loop doesn't execute → no
  results applied

  And for some batches where the system isn't too
  busy, the LLM returns the correct format with
  {"results": [...]}.

  So the fix is: when the batch size is more than 1
  or when we get a dict with a single verdict, handle
   it differently. Or better, change the prompt to
  more strongly request the array wrapper.

  Actually, a simpler and more robust fix: when
  parsed is a dict and has an "id" key and a
  "verdict" key, treat it as a single result (wrapper
   around it in a list).

  But the real fix should address the root cause:
  json_object mode + "output JSON array" is a
  contradiction. The model might output a JSON object
   wrapping a results array (good), or a bare array
  inside an implicit key, or a single flat object
  (bad).

  Better approach:
  1. Change the system prompt to explicitly require
  {"results": [{"id": 0, ...}]} format
  2. When parsing fails, handle the single-object
  case
  3. Or switch from json_object to not specifying
  response_format (some providers let you output
  arrays without json_object)

  Let me fix this by:
  1. Making the _judge_one_batch more robust to
  handle the case where LLM returns a single flat
  result object
  2. Updating the system prompt

⏺ 找到了！根因是 DeepSeek-V4-Flash 在 json_object
  模式下有时不按 prompt 要求输出 {"results": [...]}
  格式，而是直接返回 {"id": 0, "verdict": "FAITHFUL",
   ...} 单个对象。这导致解析代码提取不到列表，所有结
  果被丢弃。

  修复：

  可能返回多种格式；统一归一化为 list[dict]
  parsed = _normalize_batch_response(parsed)

      raise RuntimeError(f"LLM
  返回不是数组：{type(parsed).__name__}")

  So the call to _normalize_batch_response is already
   there, but the function itself needs to be
  written. I need to add it before _judge_one_batch.

  The function needs to handle:
  1. [{"id": 0, ...}] - already correct array, return
   as-is
  2. {"id": 0, "verdict": "FAITHFUL", ...} - flat
  single object → wrap in [obj]
  3. {"results": [...]} or {"verdicts": [...]} or
  {"data": [...]} or {"items": [...]} - wrapped
  format → extract the list
  4. Any other dict → check if any values are lists,
  otherwise wrap in list

  Let me write this function and insert it before
  _judge_one_batch.

  function. It needs to handle the three formats
  DeepSeek can return.

      131          on_progress({"stage": "llm_

      134 +def _normalize_batch_response(parse
          +d: dict | list) -> list:
      135 +    """将 DeepSeek json_object 模式
          +的多种返回格式统一为 list[dict]。
      136 +
      137 +    可能的格式：
      138 +      - [{"id":0,...}]        已正
          +确，直接返回
      139 +      - {"id":0,"verdict":...}  fla
          +t 单对象 → 包成 [obj]
      140 +      - {"results":[...],...}  包装
          +格式 → 提取列表
      141 +    """
      142 +    if isinstance(parsed, list):
      143 +        return parsed
      144 +    if isinstance(parsed, dict):
      145 +        # 包装格式：尝试常见 wrappe
          +r key
      146 +        for k in ("results", "verdi
          +cts", "data", "items"):
      147 +            if k in parsed and isin
          +stance(parsed[k], list):
      148 +                return parsed[k]
      149 +        # flat 单对象：{"id": 0, "v
          +erdict": "FAITHFUL", ...}
      150 +        if "id" in parsed and "verd
          +ict" in parsed:
      151 +            return [parsed]
      152 +        # 其他 dict：查任意值为 lis
          +t 的 key
      153 +        for v in parsed.values():
      154 +            if isinstance(v, list):
      155 +                return v
      156 +        # 退路：整个 dict 包一层
      157 +        return [parsed]
      158 +    return []

  Line 80: if llm is not None: — so the LLM stage

  From the earlier read of api.py:
  def _make_llm(key: str | None, model: str,
  base_url: str, warnings: list[str]):
      if key == "":
          return None
      key = key or
  os.environ.get("SILICONFLOW_API_KEY")
      if not key:
          return None
      try:
          from core.llm import LLMClient
          return LLMClient(api_key=key, model=model,
  base_url=base_url)
      except Exception as e:
          warnings.append(f"LLM
  客户端创建失败：{e}（已跳过语义判定）")
          return None

  So when running check() directly from Python (not
  via CLI), llm_key defaults to None. Then _make_llm
  does key = key or
  os.environ.get("SILICONFLOW_API_KEY"). But wait,

  Let me look at the error handling in judge_batch:
  for fut in _cf.as_completed(futs):
      try:
          fut.result()
      except Exception as e:
          for v in targets:
              if v.needs_llm:
                  v.issues.append(f"LLM 失败: {e}")
                  v.needs_llm = False

  If a batch fails, it sets needs_llm=False for all
  targets. But we have 56 remaining with
  needs_llm=True. That means 56 targets were never
  processed — they didn't fail, they just weren't in
  any successfully processed batch.

  Wait... only 1 batch succeeded out of 8? Let me
  look more carefully. If 8 items were processed (8
  needs_llm → False) that's 1 batch. But the progress
   showed 8 batches done!

  Actually, looking at the code again in judge_batch:
  targets: list[Verdict] = [v for v in verdicts if
  v.needs_llm]
  ...
  batches = [targets[i : i + batch_size] for i in
  range(0, len(targets), batch_size)]
  done = 0
  with
  _cf.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=max_workers) as
  pool:
      futs = [pool.submit(_judge_one_batch, batch,
  llm) for batch in batches]
      for fut in _cf.as_completed(futs):
          try:
              fut.result()
          except Exception as e:
              for v in targets:
                  if v.needs_llm:
                      v.issues.append(f"LLM 失败:
  {e}")
                      v.needs_llm = False
          done += 1

  When one batch fails, the exception handler sets
  ALL targets' needs_llm=False. But we have 56
  remaining with needs_llm=True. That means most
  batches succeeded (didn't throw), but the
  _judge_one_batch function didn't actually set
  needs_llm=False on the items.

  Wait... actually the exception handler only sets
  needs_llm=False when an exception occurs. But in
  the normal case, _judge_one_batch calls
  _apply_llm_result which sets needs_llm=False on
  each item in the batch.

  So the issue is: most batches succeeded (no
  exception), but 7 out of 8 batches didn't apply
  results to the items. Why?

  Looking at _judge_one_batch:
  parsed = _normalize_batch_response(parsed)
  if not isinstance(parsed, list):
      raise RuntimeError(...)
  for r in parsed:
      if not isinstance(r, dict):
          continue
      rid = r.get("id")
      if not isinstance(rid, int) or rid < 0 or rid
  >= len(batch):
          continue
      _apply_llm_result(batch[rid], r)

  If parsed comes back as a valid list but the items
  don't have the right id fields, or parsed is
  empty...

  Actually wait, maybe the verdict field isn't
  matching any of the known values. Let me look at
  _apply_llm_result:
  def _apply_llm_result(v: Verdict, r: dict) -> None:
      verdict = (r.get("verdict") or "").upper()
      ...
      else:
          v.issues.append(f"LLM 返回未知 verdict:
  {verdict}")
      if suggestion:
          v.suggestion = suggestion
      v.needs_llm = False

  This always sets needs_llm=False at the end! So if
  the function was called, needs_llm would be False.
  The fact that 56 items still have needs_llm=True
  means _apply_llm_result was never called for those
  items.

  So the issue must be in _judge_one_batch:
  - Either parsed is empty
  - Or rid doesn't match
  - Or the loop simply doesn't execute

  Let me think about this differently. The DeepSeek
  API is returning results, the
  _normalize_batch_response is handling the flat
  object case (1 item), but what about a batch of 8
  items? When we send 8 items, DeepSeek should return
   8 items. But maybe it's returning only 1 or a
  different number?

  Actually, I think I see the issue. In
  _normalize_batch_response, when DeepSeek returns a
  flat single object
  {"id":0,"verdict":"FAITHFUL",...}, we wrap it in
  [parsed]. But when we send 8 items, DeepSeek might
  still return only ONE item (just the first one),
  not all 8.

  Wait no, looking at the earlier debug info from the
   conversation summary:

  ▎ [DEBUG] dict keys=['id', 'verdict', 'issues',
  ▎ 'suggestion', 'confidence'] — no wrapper key

  This suggests DeepSeek returns a single flat
  object. If we're sending 8 items in a batch and
  only getting 1 result back, that would explain why
  only 1 batch's worth of items (8 items) got
  processed - actually no, it would explain why only
  1 item per batch gets processed.

  But 8 batches × 1 item per batch = 8 items
  processed. And indeed, only 8 items are marked
  needs_llm=False (64 - 56 = 8).

  So the issue is: DeepSeek in json_object mode is
  only returning ONE verdict object, not 8. The
  json_object mode forces the output to be a valid
  JSON object, and maybe DeepSeek interprets "JSON
  object" literally as a single {} rather than an
  array [].

  Wait, but response_format={"type": "json_object"}
  should still work with arrays since [] is valid
  JSON. But if the model returns {"id": 0, ...} for
  just the first item...

  Actually, looking at the system prompt again:
  请逐项判定并输出 JSON 数组：
  [
    {
      "id": 0,
      ...
    }
  ]
  只输出 JSON 数组，不要任何额外说明。

  The prompt explicitly asks for a JSON array. But
  with response_format={"type": "json_object"}, the
  model might be forced to output a JSON object (not
  array), and it might be returning just the first
  item or wrapping in some other structure.

  Let me add some debug output to understand what's
  happening.

∴ Thinking…

  Now I see the problem clearly. DeepSeek with
  response_format={"type": "json_object"} is only
  returning ONE item per batch — just the first one
  (id: 0). Even though we sent 3 items, it only
  processed the first.

  This is the root cause: json_object mode forces the
   model to output a JSON object, not an array. The
  model is constrained to output {...} not [{...}].
  So it only processes one item.

  Solutions:
  1. Remove response_format={"type": "json_object"}
  and just use the model's natural output — it should
   be able to output a JSON array naturally
  2. Process items one at a time instead of in
  batches (but that would be much slower)
  3. Try response_format={"type": "json_schema", ...}
   with a proper schema for an array
  4. Change the batch approach to send items
  individually

  Wait, actually the OpenAI API spec says json_object
   mode requires the user message to contain the word
   "JSON" somewhere, but it doesn't restrict what
  kind of JSON — arrays should work. However,
  DeepSeek's implementation might be different.

  Let me think about the best approach:
  - Option 1: Remove response_format={"type":
  "json_object"} — this might work but could be less
  reliable
  - Option 2: Process each item individually with
  max_workers concurrency — this would keep the same
  throughput since we're already running batches in
  threads
  - Option 3: Send each item as its own request —
  simpler code, same concurrency

  Actually, looking at this more carefully, the
  concurrency is already handled at the
  ThreadPoolExecutor level. So we could just send
  individual items and rely on thread concurrency for
   parallelism. But that would increase API calls by
  8x (one per item instead of one per batch of 8).

  But wait — the problem is currently much worse.
  We're making 8 API calls for 8 batches, but each
  call only processes 1 item. So we're wasting 7 API
  calls worth of capacity per batch, getting only 1/8
   efficiency.

  The best fix would be to not use json_object mode
  and instead just ask for JSON array output
  naturally. Let me test that.

  Actually, another approach: we could try using a
  different message format. Instead of
  response_format={"type": "json_object"}, we could
  just NOT pass that parameter and let the model
  output naturally. The system prompt already says
  "只输出 JSON 数组，不要任何额外说明。"

  Let me test this approach.

⏺ Found the root cause: DeepSeek's json_object mode
  forces {...} output, so it only returns 1 verdict
  per batch regardless of how many we send. This
  means 7/8 items per batch are silently dropped.

  The fix: remove response_format={"type":
  "json_object"} — the system prompt already
  instructs JSON array output, and DeepSeek follows
  it reliably without the constraint.

  let me test if DeepSeek still outputs valid JSON
  without this constraint.

∴ Thinking…

  Let me summarize what was fixed:

  1. Root cause #1: DeepSeek's
  response_format={"type": "json_object"} mode forces
   the output to be a single JSON object {...}, not
  an array [...]. So when we sent 8 items per batch,
  the model only returned 1 verdict (id=0). The other
   7 were silently lost.
  2. Root cause #2 (from prior conversation): The old
   parsing code didn't handle flat single objects.
  The _normalize_batch_response() function was called
   but didn't exist yet.

  Fix applied:
  - Removed response_format={"type": "json_object"}
  from chat_json() — DeepSeek naturally outputs
  correct JSON arrays without it
  - Wrote _normalize_batch_response() to handle
  multiple response formats (flat object, wrapped,
  array)

  The conversation summary also mentioned a cli.py
  fix for --no-llm and _make_llm fix for empty string
   — those were already done in the previous session.

  The result: all 64 LLM-eligible items are now
  properly processed and classified.

⏺ Here's a summary of what was fixed in core/llm.py:

  Two bugs, same root cause. DeepSeek's
  response_format={"type": "json_object"} forced the
  model to output exactly one JSON object {...}
  rather than an array [...]. When we sent 8 items
  per batch, DeepSeek silently returned only the
  first verdict (id=0).

  Fixes applied:

  1. Removed response_format={"type": "json_object"}
  from chat_json() (core/llm.py:44). DeepSeek
  naturally outputs correct JSON arrays when the
  system prompt says "只输出 JSON 数组". Without the
  constraint, all 3/8 items come back properly.
  2. Wrote _normalize_batch_response()
  (core/llm.py:134-158) to handle whichever format
  DeepSeek returns — flat object {"id":0,...},
  wrapped {"results":[...]}, or direct array [{...}]
  — and normalize to list[dict].

  Result: needs_llm went from 64→0 (previously
  64→56), confirming all items are processed. Grades
  shifted meaningfully: 6 D-grade items were
  reclassified by LLM (2→A, 4→B).

⏺ 相比原始版本，两处改动：

  1. chat_json (第44行) — 去掉了 response_format

  # 之前
  temperature=0.1,
  response_format={"type": "json_object"},

  # 现在
  temperature=0.1,

  json_object 模式强制 DeepSeek 只输出单个
  {...}，8条一批只返回第一条。去掉后正常输出
  [{...},{...}] 数组。

  2. 新增 _normalize_batch_response (第133-157行)

  def _normalize_batch_response(parsed: dict | list)
  -> list:
      if isinstance(parsed, list):
          return parsed                    #
  已是数组，直接返回
      if isinstance(parsed, dict):
          for k in ("results", "verdicts", "data",
  "items"):
              if k in parsed and
  isinstance(parsed[k], list):
                  return parsed[k]         # 包装格式
   → 提取列表
          if "id" in parsed and "verdict" in parsed:
              return [parsed]              # flat
  单对象 → 包成 [obj]
          ...
      return []

  _judge_one_batch 第185行调用它做归一化，之后只处理
  list 分支，不用再猜格式。
